рдЗрддреНрдпреБрдХреНрддрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рдЗрджрдордкрд┐ рд╡реИрд╢реНрд╡рджреЗрд╡рдореН ред тАШрддрдореБ рд╖реНрдЯреБрд╣рд┐’ рдЗрддреНрдпреЗрдХрд╛рджрд╢реА рд░реБрджреНрд░рджреЗрд╡рддреНрдпрд╛ ред рд╕рдкреНрддрджрд╢реНрдпреЗрдХрдкрджрд╛ ’ рдПрддрдпреЛрд░реБрдкрд╛рдиреНрддреНрдпреИрдХрдкрджрд╛’ рдЗрддреНрдпрдиреБрдХреНрд░рдорд┐рд╖реНрдпрдорд╛рдгрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН ред рдЕрддреНрд░рд╛рдиреБрдХреНрд░рдордгрд┐рдХрд╛-тАЩрдкреНрд░ рд╢рдВрддрдорд╛ рджреНрд╡реНрдпреВрдиреИрдХрд╛рджрд╢реА рд░реМрджреНрд░реА ’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧреЛ рд▓реИрдЩреНрдЧрд┐рдХрдГ рее

Jamison Brereton

42 (396)
All Gods
Atri Bhauma
18 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh, except ekapad─Б vir─Бj 17
Like the last hymn, this one enumerates a number of different gods to whom we direct our praise, beginning, as V.41 did, with Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, and the concern, as in that hymn, is generally the ritual exchange of mortal praise for immortal gifts. Or such is the structure of the opening (vss. 1тАУ6) and concluding (vss. 11тАУ18) sec
tions of the hymn. In the middle (vss. 7тАУ10) Br╠еhaspati (in vs. 10 with the Maruts) is called upon to be generous to generous patrons but to unleash destructive power against stingy patrons and non-sacrificers. As Hanns-Peter Schmidt has noted, these hostile actions are uncharacteristic of Br╠еhaspati but typical of Indra, just as the association of Indra with the sacred formulation in verse 4 would be more expected of Br╠еhaspati than Indra. He therefore argues (1968: 84тАУ86) that verses 4тАУ10 form a unity in this hymn, with Br╠еhaspati serving as an epithet of Indra.
Although the gods in the enumerative verses are often named, some verses are riddles, describing the god without naming him (1cd, 6, 13, 14) or naming him only in the second half of the verse (3, 11). Such puzzles are common in All God hymns.
At the end of the hymn (vss. 14тАУ17) the poet expresses the hope that his praise should reach in all directions, to all three worlds, creating wide space for him and his companions (in the final single-p─Бda verse 17). (Verse 18 is adopted from A┼Ыvin hymns later in the maс╣Зс╕Нala [V.76.5, 77.5], perhaps to introduce the A┼Ыvins, who are otherwise unmentioned, into this All God hymn.)

Jamison Brereton Notes

All Gods As noted in the published introduction, like V.41 this hymn enumerates a number of divine dedicands with no apparent ordering, save for the middle vss. (7-9), where Bс╣Ыhaspati dominates. The list includes 1 Varuс╣Зa, Mitra, Bhaga, Aditi, Aryaman / 2 Aditi, Mitra and Varuс╣Зa / 3 Savitar / 4 Indra / 5 Bhaga, Savitar, Aс╣Г┼Ыa, V─Бja, and Puraс╣Гdhi / 6 Indra / 7-8 (-9) Brhaspati ╠е / 10 Maruts / 11 Rudra / 12 Sarasvat─л, Brhaddiv ╠е ─Б, R─Бk─Б / 13 Tvaс╣гс╣нar (+ Vi┼Ыvar┼лpa?) / 14 Parjanya / 15 Maruts / 16 Earth (etc.) / 17 gods / 18 A┼Ыvins. Note no Agni, unless he’s hidden in 1cd. The hymn is much more straightforward, and less interesting, than V.41, but provides a relaxing interlude in the overheated rhetoric of the All God hymns of V.

рд╢рдВрддрдорд╛ рдЕрддреНрдпрдиреНрддрдВ рд╕реБрдЦрдХрд░реА рдЧреАрдГ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рд░реВрдкрд╛ рд╡рд╛рдХреН рд╡рд░реБрдгрдВ рдорд┐рддреНрд░рдВ рднрдЧрдорджрд┐рддрд┐рдВ рдЪ рджреАрдзрд┐рддреА рджреАрдзрд┐рддреНрдпрд╛ рдХрд░реНрдордгрд╛ рд╣рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдкреНрд░рдХреНрд╖реЗрдкрдгрд╛рддреНрдордХреЗрди рд╕рд╣ рдиреВрдирдореН рдЕрд╡рд┐рддрдердВ рдкреНрд░ рдЕрд╢реНрдпрд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрддреБ ред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рдкреГрд╖рджреНрдпреЛрдирд┐рдГ рдкреГрд╖рджреНрд╡рд░реНрдгрд╛рдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╕реНрдердГ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╣реЛрддрд╛ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╡рд┐рдзрд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдкрд╛рдирд╛рджрд┐рд╣реЛрдорд╕реНрдп рд╕рд╛рдзрдХреЛ рд╡рд╛рдпреБрдГ ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╣реЛрддреЗрддрд┐ рд╡рд╛рдпреЛрд░реНрдирд╛рдо ред рд╡рд╛рдпреБрдГ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╕ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрдГ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╣рд┐ рд╢реНрд░реБрддреЗрдГ ред рд╕ рдЪ рдЕрддреВрд░реНрддрдкрдиреНрдерд╛рдГ рдЕрд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рд┐рддрдЧрддрд┐рдГ рдЕрд╕реБрд░рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╕реНрдп рджрд╛рддрд╛ рдордпреЛрднреБрдГ рд╕реБрдЦрд╕реНрдпрд╛рд╕реНрдкрджрднреВрддрдГ ред рдПрд╡рдореБрдХреНрддрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгреЛ рд╡рд╛рдпреБрдГ рд╢реГрдгреЛрддреБ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░рдорд┐рддрд┐ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay our most animating praise, together with our offerings, successfully attain Varuс╣Зa, Mitra, Bhaga and Aditi; may the ministrant of the five (vital airs, V─Бyu), the dweller in the dappled (firmament), he whose path is unimpeded, who is the giver of life, the bestower of happiness, hear.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

May the most availing hymn now reach Varuс╣Зa with its visionary power; may it reach Mitra, Bhaga, Aditi.
Let him hear itтАФthe lord whose womb is the dappled (cow/ghee), who has five Hotars, whose path cannot be transgressed, who is joy itself [=Aryaman].

Jamison Brereton Notes

As Geldner (etc.) point out, ├бt┼лrtapanth─Бс╕е is the clue to the identification of the referent of cd, since this epithet only occurs once elsewhere in the RV, in X.64.5, where it is explicitly used of Aryaman. In that passage he is also qualified as sapt├бhot─Б тАШhaving 7 HotrarsтАЩ, like p├б├▒cahot─Б here. And of course Aryaman makes sense in this highly ─Аdityan context. Nonetheless, I think p─Бda c (pс╣Ы╠Бс╣гadyoniс╕е p├б├▒cahot─Б) flirts with a different identification – of Agni – before sealing that of Aryaman by ├бt┼лrtapanth─Бс╕е in d. Agni could plausibly have a womb of dappled (ghee) (pс╣Ы╠Бс╣гadyoni-), similar to ghс╣Ыt├бyoni- тАШhaving a womb of gheeтАЩ used of Agni in V.8.6, as Geldner points out (n. 1cd), and of course Agni is both associated with Hotars and is the Hotar par excellence himself. Since, as noted above, Agni is not otherwise found in this hymn, the poet may have gestured towards him covertly in 1c.

Griffith

Now may our sweetest song with deep devotion reach Varuna, Mitra, Aditi, and Bhaga.
May the Five Priests’ Lord, dwelling in oblations, bliss-giving Asura, hear, whose paths are open.

Geldner

Als die genehmste m├╢ge nunmehr unsere Lobrede mit Andacht zu Varuna, Mitra, Bhaga, Aditi dringen. Der erfreuliche Asura, der in Schmalz sitzt und f├╝nf Opferpriester hat, der seinen Weg noch nicht zur├╝ckgelegt hat, soll zuh├╢ren.

Grassmann

Vor dringe nun das liebste Lied mit Andacht zu Aditi, Varuna, Mitra, Bhaga, Es h├╢r, der wohlthut, dem f├╝nf Priester dienen, der Gott mit Gut im Schooss, dess Pfad unnahbar.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay Aditi accept my affectionate and devoted praise, as a mother (the endearments of) a son; the plural asing, delightful prayer that is approved of by the gods I address to Varuс╣Зa and Mitra.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

May Aditi grab hold of my praise, like a mother the beloved son of her heart.
The dear sacred formulation that has been established by the gods, that is joy itself to Mitra and Varuс╣ЗaтАФmay I (grab hold of it).

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. is quite straightforward until we reach p─Бda d, where the nom. ah├бm тАШIтАЩ demands a verb that isnтАЩt there. Keeping in mind the theme of divine/human reciprocity that runs through the last hymn and the rest of this one and employing our usual method of attempting to supply missing material from context, it seems best to supply a form of pr├бti тИЪgrabh complementary to pr├бti тАж jagс╣Ыbhy─Бt in a with Aditi as subject. The poet wishes to grasp the br├бhman- produced by the gods (c) in order to turn it into praise (st├│ma-) for the gods (a). This reciprocal relationship may be signaled by the first word in the vs. pr├бti тАШin return, in responseтАЩ.

The other question in d is what to do with the untethered locc. mitr├й varuс╣З├й. I have followed Geldner in loosely construing them with mayobh├║ тАШjoy itselfтАЩ, even though this stem does not elsewhere take a loc. Geldner (n. 2d) cites a series of parallels with locc.

mitr├й v├бruс╣Зe that seem to have similarly loose beneficial value.

Griffith

May Aditi welcome, even as a mother her dear heart-gladdening son, my song that lauds her.
The prayer they love, bliss-giving, God-appointed, I offer unto Varuna and Mitra.

Geldner

Aditi soll meinen Lobgesang wie die Mutter ihren Herzenssohn, den Liebling aufnehmen; ich m├╢chte das liebe Kraftwort, das gottverliehene, das f├╝r Mitra und Varuna erfreulich ist, empfangen.

Grassmann

Mein Loblied m├╢ge Aditi ergreifen, so wie den holden Herzenssohn die Mutter, Das labende, das liebe, gottbefohlne Gebet bring’ ich dem Varuna und Mitra.

Elizarenkova

рдЕрдирдпрд╛ рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЪ рд╕реНрддреВрдпрддреЗ ред рд╣реЗ рдЛрддреНрд╡рд┐рдЬрдГ рдХрд╡реАрдирд╛рдВ рдХрд╡рд┐рддрдордВ рдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрджрд░реНрд╢рд┐рдирдореН рдЕрдореБрдВ рдкреБрд░реЛрд╡рд░реНрддрд┐рдирдордЧреНрдирд┐рдВ рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛рд░рдВ рд╡рд╛ рдЙрджреАрд░рдп рдКрд░реНрдзреНрд╡рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдпрдд рд╣рд░реНрд╖рдпрддреЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдПрдирдВ рджреЗрд╡рдВ рдордзреНрд╡рд╛ рдордзреБрд░реЗрдг рд╕реЛрдорд░рд╕реЗрди рдШреГрддреЗрди рдЪ рдЕрднрд┐ рдЙрдирддреНрдд рдЕрднрд┐рд╖рд┐рдЮреНрдЪрдд ред рддрд░реНрдкрдпрддреЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рд╕рдГ рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рджреЗрд╡рдГ рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдВ рд╡рд╕реВрдирд┐ рдирд┐рд╡рд╛рд╕рдпреЛрдЧреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐ рдЧрд╡рд╛рджрд┐рдзрдирд╛рдирд┐ рдкреНрд░рдпрддрд╛ рдкреНрд░рдпрддрд╛рдирд┐ рд╣рд┐рддрд╛рдирд┐ рдЪрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рдЖрд╣реНрд▓рд╛рджрдХрд╛рдирд┐ рд╣рд┐рд░рдгреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐ рд╕реБрд╡рд╛рддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рдпрдЪреНрдЫрддреНрд╡рд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬCelebrate, (priests), the most prophetic of the prophets; imbue him with the sweet libation, and may the divine Savit─Б bestow upon us ample, beneficial and delightful riches.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The most prophetic of the prophets: kavitamam kav─лn─Бm: kavi = kr─Бnta dar’─л, a seer or shower of the past, whence may be inferred the application of his knowledge to the future

Jamison Brereton

Rouse the best poet of poets. Wet him with honey, with ghee.
HeтАФgod SavitarтАФwill propel to us the golden goods that have been held forth and set out.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the distinction in no. between the two 2nd ps. impvs. in ab: sg. ├║d ─лraya and pl. un├бtta. As commonly, the sg. is probably a self-addressed by the poet to himself; that his object is тАЬthe best poet of poetsтАЭ (kav├нtamaс╣Г kav─лn─Б╠Бm) simply emphasizes the closed loop of reciprocity. The pl. impv. is presumably addressed to his fellow celebrants, in this case the priests charged with the physical activity (the Adhvaryu and his helpers, quite possibly). The pl. impv. un├бtta has a strong stem form where we properly expect weak, but the expected form *und-ta ├а *untta ├а (probably simplified to) *unta would have been difficult to parse.

Griffith

In spirit him, the Sagest of the Sages; with sacrificial oil and meath bedew him
So then let him, God Savitar, provide us excellent, ready, and resplendent treasures.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдлрд┐рд░ рдЙрд╕реА рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХреЛ рдХрд╣рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛ ! рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рдЦреЗрдд рдмреЛрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдЬрди (рдордзреНрд╡рд╛) рдордзреБрд░ (рдШреГрддреЗрди) рдЬрд▓ рд╕реЗ рдХреНрд╖реЗрддреНрд░ рдЖрджрд┐ рд╕реАрдВрдЪ рдХрд░ рдЕрдиреНрдирд╛рджрд┐рдХреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рд╣реА (рдПрдирдореН) рдЗрд╕ (рдХрд╡реАрдирд╛рдореН) рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐рдорд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдордзреНрдп рдореЗрдВ (рдХрд╡рд┐рддрдордореН) рдЕрддреНрдпрдиреНрдд рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐рдорд╛рдиреН рдХреЛ (рдЙрддреН, рдИрд░рдп) рдЙрддреНрддрдорддрд╛ рд╕реЗ рдкреНрд░реЗрд░рдгрд╛ рджреЗрдУ рддрдерд╛ (рдЕрднрд┐, рдЙрдирддреНрдд) рдЕрднреНрдпреБрджрдп рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдФрд░ рдЙрддреНрддрдо рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рд╕реЗ рд╕реАрдВрдЪреЛ рдФрд░ рд╣реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рдиреН ! рдЬрд┐рд╕ рдХрд╡рд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдордзреНрдп рдореЗрдВ рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрда рдХрд╡рд┐ рдХреА рдкреНрд░реЗрд░рдгрд╛ рдХрд░реЛ (рд╕рдГ) рд╡рд╣ (рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдФрд░ рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдп рдХрд╛ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ (рджреЗрд╡рдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН (рдирдГ) рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рдкреНрд░рдпрддрд╛) рдкреНрд░рдпрддреНрди рд╕реЗ рд╕рд┐рджреНрдз рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп (рдЪрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐) рдЖрдирдиреНрдж рдХреЗ рджреЗрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рд╕реБрд╡рд░реНрдг рдЖрджрд┐ (рд╣рд┐рддрд╛рдирд┐) рд╣рд┐рддрдХрд╛рд░рдХ (рд╡рд╕реВрдирд┐) рджреНрд░рд╡реНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рд╕реБрд╡рд╛рддрд┐) рджреЗрд╡реЗ реерейрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЕрдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖реЛ ! рдЖрдк рд▓реЛрдЧ рдЬреЛ рдирд┐рд╢реНрдЪрдп рдХрд░рдХреЗ рд╕рдм рд╕реЗ рдЙрддреНрддрдо, рд╕рдореНрдкреВрд░реНрдг рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдУрдВ рд╕реЗ рдпреБрдХреНрдд, рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрда рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╣реЛрд╡реЗ, рдЙрд╕рдХреЛ рдЧреГрд╣рд╛рд╢реНрд░рдо рди рдХрд░, рдРрд╕рд╛ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢ рджреАрдЬрд┐рдпреЗред рдЬрд┐рд╕рд╕реЗ рд╕рдВрд╕рд╛рд░ рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рди рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рдмреЬрд╛ рд╕реБрдЦ рдмреЭреЗ, рдХреНрдпреЛрдВрдХрд┐ рдЬреЛ рдирд┐рд╢реНрдЪрдп рдХрд░рдХреЗ рдкреВрд░реНрдг рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдпреБрдХреНрдд рд╣реЛрдХрд░ рдЧреГрд╣рд╛рд╢реНрд░рдо рдХреЛ рдХрд░реЗ, рд╡рд╣ рдмрд╣реБрдд рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкрд╛рд░рд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рд╕реЗ, рд╡реАрд░реНрдпреНрдп рдЖрджрд┐ рдХреЗ рдирд╛рд╢ рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рд╕реЗ, рдереЛреЬреА рдЕрд╡рд╕реНрдерд╛рдпреБрдХреНрдд рд╣реЛрдХрд░ рдирд┐рд░рдиреНрддрд░ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╣рд┐рдд рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдХреЛ рдирд╣реАрдВ рд╕рдорд░реНрде рд╣реЛрд╡реЗ реерейрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ ! рдпрдерд╛ рдХреГрд╖реАрд╡рд▓рд╛ рдордзреНрд╡рд╛ рдШреГрддреЗрди рдХреНрд╖реЗрддреНрд░рд╛рджреАрдирд┐ рд╕рд┐рдХреНрддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╢рд╕реНрдпрд╛рджреАрдирд┐ рд▓рднрдиреНрддреЗ рддрдереИрд╡реИрдирдВ рдХрд╡реАрдирд╛рдВ рдХрд╡рд┐рддрдордореБрджреАрд░рдпрд╛рднреНрдпреБрджрдпрд╛рдпреЛрдирддреНрддред рд╣реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕реЛ ! рдпрдВ рдХрд╡реАрдирд╛рдВ рдХрд╡рд┐рддрдордореБрджреАрд░рдп рд╕ рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рджреЗрд╡реЛ рдиреЛ рдкреНрд░рдпрддрд╛ рдЪрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рд╣рд┐рддрд╛рдирд┐ рд╡рд╕реВрдирд┐ рд╕реБрд╡рд╛рддрд┐ реерейрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЙрддреН) (рдИрд░рдп) рдкреНрд░реЗрд░рдпрдд (рдХрд╡рд┐рддрдордореН) рдЕрддрд┐рд╢рдпреЗрди рдореЗрдзрд╛рд╡рд┐рдирдореН (рдХрд╡реАрдирд╛рдореН) рдореЗрдзрд╛рд╡рд┐рдирд╛рдореН (рдЙрдирддреНрдд) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╕реБрд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рд╕рд┐рдЮреНрдЪрдд (рдПрдирдореН) (рдЕрднрд┐) рдЖрднрд┐рдореБрдЦреНрдпреЗ (рдордзреНрд╡рд╛) рдордзреБрд░реЗрдг (рдШреГрддреЗрди) рдЙрджрдХреЗрдиреЗрд╡ (рд╕рдГ) (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдореН (рд╡рд╕реВрдирд┐) рджреНрд░рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдгрд┐ (рдкреНрд░рдпрддрд╛) рдкреНрд░рдпрддреНрдирд╕рд╛рдзреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐ (рд╣рд┐рддрд╛рдирд┐) рд╣рд┐рддрдХрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ (рдЪрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐) рдЖрдирдиреНрджрдкреНрд░рджрд╛рдирд┐ рд╕реБрд╡рд░реНрдгрд╛рджреАрдирд┐ (рджреЗрд╡рдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН (рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдпрдХрд╛рд░рдХрдГ (рд╕реБрд╡рд╛рддрд┐) рд╕реБрд╡реЗрддреН рдкреНрд░рдпрдЪреНрдЫреЗрддреН реерейрее

рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рдордирд╕рд╛ рдкреНрд░рдХреГрд╖реНрдЯреЗрди рдЪреЗрддрд╕рд╛ рдЧреЛрднрд┐рдГ рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдВ рдиреЗрд╖рд┐ рдирдпрд╕рд┐ ред рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рдЧрд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдпрд╕реАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдПрд╡рдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреНрд░ ред рд╣реЗ рд╣рд░рд┐рд╡рдГ рд╣рд░рд┐рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рддрджреНрд╡рдиреН рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рд╕реВрд░рд┐рднрд┐рдГ рдореЗрдзрд╛рд╡рд┐рднрд┐рдГ рдкреБрддреНрд░реИрд░реНрдЛрддреНрд╡рд┐рдЧреНрднрд┐рд░реНрд╡рд╛ рд╕рдВ рдиреЗрд╖рд┐ ред рддрдерд╛ рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрддрд┐ рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рдХреНрд╖реЗрдореИрдГ рд╕рдВ рдиреЗрд╖рд┐ ред рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордгрд╛ рдкреНрд░рднреВрддреЗрдирд╛рдиреНрдиреЗрди рд╕рдВ рдиреЗрд╖рд┐ ред рдпрддреН рдЕрдиреНрдирдВ рджреЗрд╡рд╣рд┐рддрдореН рдЕрд╕реНрддрд┐ рддреЗрди ред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд┐рдпрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рд░реНрд╣рд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╕реБрдорддреНрдпрд╛ рдЕрдиреБрдЧреНрд░рд╣рдмреБрджреНрдзреНрдпрд╛ рд╕рдВ рдиреЗрд╖рд┐ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWith a (willing) mind, Indra, you associate us with cattle, with pious (priests) and, lord of steeds, with prosperity, with (sacrificial) food that is agreeable to the gods, and with the favour of the adorable deities.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Yajus. 2.15

Jamison Brereton

Through your thought, Indra, join us with cows, with patrons, with well-being, o possessor of the fallow baysтАФ
and with the sacred formulation established by the gods, with the favor of the gods who are worthy of the sacrifice.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner thinks itтАЩs our m├бnas- thatтАЩs at issue, but context makes it more likely to be IndraтАЩs (so also Renou and Witzel Got┼Н).

P─Бda c is a minor variant of 2c and in fact makes clear what the structure of 2c is and where the rel. cl. begins. A minor example of syntactic repair.

Griffith

With willing mind, Indra, vouchsafe us cattle, prosperity, Lord of Bays! and pious patrons;
And, with the sacred prayer by Gods appointed, give us the holy Deities’ lovingkindness.

Geldner

Verhilf uns, Indra, durch unsere Einsicht zu K├╝hen, zu freigebigen Herren, o Falbenlenker, zu Gl├╝ck, zu dem Kraftwort, das gottverliehen ist, zur Gunst der opferw├╝rdigen G├╢tter.

Grassmann

Beschenk uns, Indra, holden Sinns mit Rindern, mit reichen Gebern und mit Heil, o Rossherr, Mit solchen Bitten, die der Gott uns eingibt, und mit der Gunst der opferwerthen G├╢tter.

English translation:

тАЬMay the divine Bhaga, Savit─Б, the lord of wealth, Aс╣Г┼Ыa, Indra (the slayer) of Vс╣Ыtra, (all) the conquerors of riches, с╣Ъbhukс╣гin, V─Бja and also Purandhi, immortals, hastening (to our sacrifice) preserve us.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

с╣Ъbhukс╣гin: a name of Indra, but here it implies с╣Ъbhu, while Purandhi = Vibhu, making, with V─Бja, the triad. Aс╣Г┼Ыa is an apparent reference to Soma

Jamison Brereton

God Bhaga, Savitar, Share of Wealth [/Aс╣Г┼Ыa], Indra, the complete victor over Vr╠еtra and riches,
the lord of the R╠еbhus, V─Бja [=a R╠еbhu], and PlenitudeтАФlet the powerful immortals aid us.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In p─Бda a it is unclear with what noun to construe gen. r─Бy├бс╕е. Geldner and Renou take it with savit─Б╠Б(Geldner: тАЬder Zuweiser тАж des ReichtumsтАЭ), while Witzel Got┼Н seem to agree with me in taking it with ├бс╣Г┼Ыa(с╕е). Since Savitar is a far more defined divine being with a name that, though having the literal sense тАШimpellerтАЩ, is normally used just as a name, I think Aс╣Г┼Ыa, whose animatization is fairly shaky, is more likely to be used in a literal abstract value and construed with a gen. of the same type.

The problematic form in the vs. is saс╣Гj├нtaс╕е. Properly speaking, this should either be an abl./gen. sg. or a nom./acc. pl. of the root noun cmpd saс╣Гj├нt- тАШcomplete victorтАЩ. Grassmann analyzes it as gen. sg., modifying vс╣Ыtr├бsya, as, apparently, does Renou, while Geldner and Witzel Got┼Н take it as nom. pl., presumably applicable to all the gods listed singly before. All construe the gen. pl. dh├бn─Бn─Бm with it (e.g., Geldner тАЬdie Erbeuter der Sch├дtzeтАЭ), but this leaves vс╣Ыtr├бsya stranded, since it would be perverse to attribute the victory over Vс╣Ыtra to Bhaga, Savitar, and Aс╣Г┼Ыa in addition to Indra. Therefore all the standard tr. supply sg. *hant─Б╠Б(vel sim.) as an appositive to Indra, to govern vс╣Ыtr├бsya. I consider this unnec. Our p─Бda seems to be based on a much-repeated p─Бda, couched in the acc. sg., in the Triс╣гс╣нubh refrain vs. of the Vi┼Ыv─БmitrasтАЩ Indra hymns: III.30.22 (etc.) ghn├бntaс╣Г vс╣Ыtс╣Ы─Б╠Бс╣Зi saс╣Гj├нtaс╣Г dh├бn─Бn─Бm. I consider our p─Бda a nonce adaptation of the orig. p─Бda, construed as if orig. saс╣Гj├нtam belonged to a them. stem -

  • in other words saс╣Гj├нtaс╕е is a thematic back-formation, nom. singular, that allows the formula to remain metrical. The last part of 7b, with sg. sanit─Б╠Бraс╣Г dh├бn─Бn─Бm, gives some support to this interpr., and note that Indra alone is called jiс╣гс╣З├║- тАШvictorтАЩ in the next vs. (6a). Of course, it must be admitted that in III.30.22 vс╣Ыtr─Б╠Бс╣Зi is the obj. of a form of тИЪhan and so supplying such a form here (as the standard tr. do) also gets some support. But vс╣Ыtr├б- has been transformed from acc. (pl.) to gen. (sg.) in our passage and should be parallel to dh├бn─Бn─Бm.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWe celebrate the exploits of Marutvat, the unrecoiling, the victorious, the undecaying; neither the ancients, Maghavan, nor their successors, have attained your prowess, nor has any one recent attained it.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

We will proclaim the deeds of the one accompanied by the Maruts [=Indra], unopposable, victorious, unaging.
None previous to you, bounteous one, nor later, nor anyone at all right now has achieved your manly power.

Griffith

Let us declare his deeds, the undecaying unrivalled Victor whom the Maruts follow.
None of old times, O Maghavan, nor later, none of these days hath reached thy hero prowess.

Geldner

Wir wollen die Taten des Marutf├╝hrers verk├╝nden, des unwiderstehlichen, siegreichen, alterlosen. Weder Fr├╝here, o Gabenreicher, noch Sp├дtere, noch irgend ein Heutiger hat deine Heldenkraft erreicht.

Grassmann

Lasst preisen uns des unbesiegten Siegers, des Marutherrschers Thaten, der nie alt wird; Nicht jetzige, nicht fr├╝here, noch sp├дtre erreichten jemals deine Kraft, o m├дcht’ger.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬGlorify the first donor of precious treasure, Bс╣Ыhaspati, the distributor of riches, the bestower of great happiness upon him who recites or chants (his praise), who comes laden with ample wealth to his invoker.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Praise the first conferring of treasure; (praise) Br╠еhaspati, the winner of riches,
who, the most wealful for him who chants and praises, will come here, with many goods, to the one who repeatedly invokes (him).

Jamison Brereton Notes

The splv. ┼Ы├бmbhaviс╣гс╣нha- recalls ┼Ы├бс╣Гtama- in 1a. Both stems are reasonably well attested, though ┼Ы├бс╣Гtama- has the edge. They do not seem to be consistently distinguished in usage, but ┼Ы├бс╣Гtama- seems more common qualifying inanimates while ┼Ы├бmbhaviс╣гс╣нha- and its base ┼Ыambh├║-/-┼л╠Б- are more common with animates. Such is the case in this hymn, where ┼Ы├бс╣Гtam─Б in 1a modifies тАШhymnтАЩ (g─л╠Бс╕е) and ┼Ы├бmbhaviс╣гс╣нhaс╕е in 7c modifies Bс╣Ыhaspati. Nonetheless, the tr. of the two forms should be harmonized.

Griffith

Praise him the Chief who gives the boon of riches, Brhaspati distributor of treasures,
Who, blessing most the man who sings and praises, comes with abundant wealth to his invoker.

Geldner

Besinge die erste Lohnspende, besinge den Brihaspati, den Gewinner von Sch├дtzen, der dem Vortragenden, dem Lobsingenden am meisten gewogen ist und zu dem Rufenden kommen m├╢ge, der Sch├дtzereiche.

Grassmann

Besinge nun die erste G├╝terspende, Brihaspati, den Geber reicher Sch├дtze, Der heilvoll ist dem S├дnger, der ihn preiset, er komme her, an G├╝tern reich, zum Beter.

Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗ рдмреГрд╣рд╕реНрдкрддреЗ рддрд╡реЛрддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛рднрд┐рдГ рд╕рдЪрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ рд╕рдВрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ рдЕрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдГ рдЕрд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рд┐рддрд╛рдГ рдордШрд╡рд╛рдирдГ рдзрдирд╡рдиреНрддрдГ рд╕реБрд╡реАрд░рд╛рдГ рд╢реЛрднрдирдкреБрддреНрд░рд╛рд╢реНрдЪ рднрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ ред рдпреЗ рддреНрд╡рджрдиреБрдЧреГрд╣реАрддрд╛рдГ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рджрд╛рдГ рдмрд╣реВрдирд╛рдорд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВ рджрд╛рддрд╛рд░рдГ рд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ ред рдЙрдд рд╡рд╛ рдЕрдерд╡рд╛ рдЧреЛрджрд╛рдГ рд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ ред рдпреЗ рдЪ рд╡рд╕реНрддреНрд░рджрд╛рдГ рд╕реБрднрдЧрд╛рдГ рд╢реЛрднрдирдзрдирд╛рдГ рд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ рддреЗрд╖реБ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗрд╖реБ рд░рд╛рдпрдГ рдзрдирд╛рдирд┐ рд╕рдВрднрд╡рдиреНрд╡рд┐рддрд┐ рд╢реЗрд╖рдГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAssociated, Bс╣Ыhaspati, with your protections, (men) are unharmed (by foes), and become opulent and blessed with descendants; may wealth devolve on those who are genitive rous, and givers of horses, of cows, of clothes.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

O Br╠еhaspati, the bounteous ones accompanied by your help, who are invulnerable and possessing good heroes,
who are givers of horses or givers of cows, who are givers of garments, the well-portioned ones [=patrons]тАФon them (confer) riches.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The standard tr. (incl. also Schmidt, Bс╣Ыhaspati und Indra 84 and Scarlatta 202) take ab as a separate nominal cl. The difference is trivial.

Less trivial is the difference between my rendering of the last part of d and that of all the others. They take subh├бg─Бs t├йс╣гu r─Б╠Бyaс╕е as the nominal main clause to the rel. cl. (y├й a┼Ыvad─Б╠Бс╕е тАж) that occupies the rest of the hemistich. Cf., e.g., Geldner тАЬdenen geh├╢ren die begl├╝ckenden Reicht├╝mer.тАЭ In contrast I take subh├бg─Бс╕е with the rel. cl., qualifying the givers, and r─Б╠Бyaс╕е as acc. pl. in the main cl., and in the main cl.

I supply a verb тАШconferтАЩ (vel sim.) extracted from ratnadh├йyam in 7a. In favor of the standard tr. are the facts that by accent r─Б╠Бyaс╕е is better analyzed as nom. than acc. (though acc. pl. so accented are not rare) and that no verb need be supplied. Although I am usually reluctant to supply material, in this case there are countervailing factors.

First, with the exception of one late passage (X.140.5), subh├бga-, which is quite well-attested, is only used of animate beings, not of wealth or the like. Moreover, the standard rendering leaves Bс╣Ыhaspati with little to do. The givers are тАЬaccompanied by your helpтАЭ (t├бvot├нbhiс╕е), but otherwise seem to do quite nicely on their own – whereas we might expect him to be acting on their material behalf by giving to them, just as in the next vs. he is asked to strip the niggardly of their possessions and do worse by other anti-ritualists. By my interpr. the vs. expresses the usual Rigvedic trickle-down theory of material redistribution: the gods give goods to the patrons of the sacrifice (kings, etc.), who then confer them on the priests and poets.

Griffith

Tended, Brhaspati, with thy protections, the princes are unharmed and girt by heroes.
Wealth that brings bliss is found among the givers of horses and of cattle and of raiment.

Geldner

Von deinen Gnaden begleitet, o Brihaspati, sind die freigebigen G├╢nner ohne Schaden, reich an t├╝chtigen Mannen, S├╢hnen; die Verschenker von Rossen oder K├╝hen und die Verschenker von Kleidern sind, denen geh├╢ren die begl├╝ckenden Reicht├╝mer.

Grassmann

Brihaspati, versehn mit deinen H├╝lfen sind unversehrt und heldenreich die F├╝rsten, Die Rosse, Rinder oder Kleider schenken; bei denen seien gabenreiche G├╝ter.

Elizarenkova

рдПрд╖рд╛рдВ рд╡рдХреНрд╖реНрдпрдорд╛рдгрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╡рд┐рддреНрддрдВ рдзрдирдВ рд╡рд┐рд╕рд░реНрдорд╛рдгрдВ рд╡рд┐рд╕рд░рдгрд╢реАрд▓рдВ рдХреГрдгреБрд╣рд┐ рдХреБрд░реБ рд╣реЗ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордгрд╕реНрдкрддреЗ рее рдПрд╖рд╛рдорд┐рддреНрдпреБрдХреНрддрдВ рдХреЗрд╖рд╛рдорд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рд╣ ред рдпреЗ рднреБрдЮреНрдЬрддреЗ рдЕрдкреГрдгрдиреНрддрдГ рдЕрдкреНрд░рдпрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрдГ ред рдХреЗрднреНрдпрдГ ред рдЙрдХреНрдереИрдГ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдкрд╛рджрдХреИрдГ рд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд░реИрд░реНрд╡рд┐рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреЗрднреНрдпрдГ рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдореН ред рддрд╛рдиреН рдЕрдкрд╡реНрд░рддрд╛рдиреН рдЕрдкрдЧрддрдХрд░реНрдордгрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╕рд╡реЗ рдЙрддреНрдкрддреНрддрд┐рдорддрд┐ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд▓реЛрдХреЗ рд╡рд╡реГрдзрд╛рдирд╛рдиреН рд╡рд░реНрдзрдорд╛рдирд╛рдиреН рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдорджреНрд╡рд┐рд╖рдГ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрджреНрд╡реЗрд╖реНрдЯреДрдиреЗ рдордиреНрддреНрд░рджреНрд╡реЗрд╖реНрдЯреДрдиреН рд╡рд╛ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╛рддреН рдпрд╡рдпрд╕реНрд╡ рдкреГрдердХреНрдХреБрд░реБ ред рдЕрдиреНрдзрдХрд╛рд░реЗ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдкрдпреЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬRender transitory the riches of those who partake of enjoyment without giving satisfaction (to those who are eminent) by holy hymns; put apart from the sun those who perform not sacred rites, and who, though prospering in their posterity, are the adversaries of prayer.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Put apart from the sun: s┼лry─Бd yavayasva, make them separate, condemn them to darkness

Jamison Brereton

Dissipate the possessions of those who benefit by our hymns without giving. Those violating the commandments, grown strong at forward thrusting, the haters of the sacred formulationтАФkeep them away from the sun.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The stilted nominal syntax with dummy verb тИЪkс╣Ы + acc. masc. abstract (visarm─Б╠Бс╣Зaс╣Г kс╣Ыс╣Зuhi, lit. тАЬmake dissipationтАЭ), which together govern a neut. acc. vitt├бm, must result from the lack of a transitive pres. to тИЪsс╣Ы тАШflow, runтАЩ – pace Narten (тАЬAi. sс╣Ы тАжтАЭ 1969: 83 and n. 16 [=KlSch 130 and n. 16]), who characterizes several forms of v├н тИЪsс╣Ы as тАЬtransitiv,тАЭ though the acc. expresses the goal/place-throughwhich, not a real transitive object.

The expression prasav├й v─Бvс╣Ыdh─Бn─Б╠Бn is not entirely clear and is variously rendered тАФ Geldner тАЬ‘die im Befehl gross sind,тАЭ Renou тАЬqui (se croyant) renforc├йs pour la comp├йtition,тАЭ Schmidt (Bс╣Ыhaspati und Indra 85) тАЬbei (unserer) Regsamkeit wachsen,тАЭ Witzel Got┼Н тАЬobwohl sie in ihrem Unterfangen erstarkt sindтАЭ тАФ differing primarily in what prasav├б- is taken to mean. By my interpr. these foes, who violate all the norms of ─Аrya society by refusing to participate in reciprocal exchange, by acting contrary to vrat├б- (the chains of command that structure ─Аrya society), and by hating the verbal formulations that express the ─Аrya view of the cosmos and their place in it, nonetheless show their strength on the attack, the forward thrust. All the tr. reflect this notion one way or another: the regretable strength of the enemies despite their antisocial behavior.

Griffith

Make their wealth flee who, through our hymns enjoying their riches, yield us not an ample guerdon.
Far from the sun keep those who hate devotion, the godless, prospering in their vocation.

Geldner

La├Я deren Besitz zerrinnen, die ohne zu spenden von unseren Lobliedern den Nutzen haben. Die Gesetzlosen, die im Befehlen gro├Я sind, die Priesterfeinde schlie├Яe von der Sonne aus!

Grassmann

Zerrinnen lasse das Verm├╢gen derer, die ohn’ Geschenk ausbeuten unsre Lieder; Die ungerechten, die auf Reichthum trotzen, der Andacht feind, schliess aus vom Licht der Sonne.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSend, Maruts, into darkness with (cars) devoid of wheels, the man who invites the r─Бkс╣гasas to the food of the gods; (him also) who reviles me when offering praise to you; while sweating, he toils (to realize) vain desires.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Whoever lauds the demons at the invitation to the gods, run him over, Maruts, with your wheel-less (chariots).
Whoever will scorn the labor of the one who labors for you, he will render his own desires empty when he sweats (at ritual labor).

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. continues the theme of the impious foe, though the divine ally the poet calls on to destroy the foe has changed from Bс╣Ыhaspati to the Maruts. Here (p─Бda a) the enemy chooses to praise demons (rakс╣г├бsaс╕е) when gods (deva-) are being invited to the ritual and (c) mocks the ritual labor of the devotee. Because of the strong association of sweat with ritual labor in the RV (see my тАЬAvestan x┼бuu─лd: A Relic of Indo-Iranian Ritual Vocabulary,тАЭ Bulletin of the Asia Institute 25 [2011 (2015),] and for тИЪ┼Ыam тАШlaborтАЩ with тИЪsvid тАШsweatтАЩ I.86.8), I assume that the enemy himself is engaging in (what we hope will be fruitless) ritual in p─Бda d, perhaps in service of the demons, not the gods (cf. p─Бda a). In post-RVic texts the Asuras would probably serve as the polar opposition to the gods, not the Rakс╣гasas, an indirect piece of evidence for the well-known fact that the Asura-Deva opposition almost entirely postdates the RV.

In the published translation ├│hate in p─Бda a is tr. as an indicative (тАШwhoever laudsтАЩ), but it should really be a subjunctive (тАЬwhoever will laudтАЭ), both on the basis of the morphology (it belongs to a root pres., whose 3rd plural is also ├│hate) and of the parallel subjunctives in the passage, cd y├бс╕е тАж nind─Бt, тАж karate.

Griffith

With wheelless chariots drive down him, O Maruts, who at the feasts of Gods regards the demons.
May he, though bathed in sweat, form empty wishes, who blames his sacred rite who toils to serve you.

Geldner

Wer bei der G├╢tterladung die Unholde lobt, auf den fahret nieder, o Marut, mit euren r├дderlosen Wagen! Wer den Opferdienst eures Dienstfertigen herabsetzt, der soll, wenn er auch sich’s hei├Я werden l├д├Яt, eitle W├╝nsche hegen.

Grassmann

Wer bei dem Festmahl auf Unholde Acht gibt, den fahrt, o Maruts, nieder ohne R├дder; Wer schm├дht die Dienste dessen, der euch dienet, dess Streben sei umsonst, wie er auch schwitze.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPraise him who has the sure arrow, the strong bow, who presides over all sanitary drugs; worship Rudra for a comprehensive and sound understanding; adore the powerful divinity with prostrations.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Praise him, who has the good arrow and the good bow, who holds sway over every healing remedy.
Sacrifice to Rudra for great benevolence; with acts of reverence offer friendship to the god, the lord.

Jamison Brereton Notes

One of the striking passages in which the same divinity, in this case Rudra, is called both dev├б- and ├бsura- (n├бmobhir dev├бm ├бsuraс╣Г duvasya тАЬwith acts of reverence offer friendship to the god, the lordтАЭ), strong evidence that the strict division and eternal enmity between Devas and Asuras in later texts has not yet developed.

Griffith

Praise him whose bow is strong and sure his arrow, him who is Lord of every balm that bealeth.
Worship thou Rudra for his great good favour: adore the Asura, God, with salutations.

Den preise, welcher sch├╢ne Pfeil und Bogen und im Besitz hat alle Arzeneien; Zu hohem Gl├╝cke huldige dem Rudra; den Gott, den Geist, verehre mit Verbeugung.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the dexterous-handed, humble-minded artist (of the gods, the с╣Ъbhus); may the wives of the showerer (Indra); may the rivers carved out by Vibhu; may Sarasvat─л and the brilliant R─Бk─Б, the illustrious granters of desires, be willing to grant us riches.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The masters of the house, the workmen who have good hands
[=R╠еbhus?], the wives of the bull, the rivers fashioned for wide
extension,
Sarasvat─л, Br╠еhaddiv─Б, and R─Бk─БтАФlet the resplendent ones, showing
favor, create a wide realm (for us).

Jamison Brereton Notes

The grammar of this vs. is quite straightforward; what difficulty it presents lies in the uncertain and permeable boundary between PNs and common noun/adjectives. In b vibhvataс╣гс╣н─Б╠Бс╕е, modifying the rivers, is universally taken as containing the PN Vibhvan, hence тАШfashioned by VibhvanтАЩ. Since the referents of p─Бda a are the с╣Ъbhus and Vibhvan is the name of an с╣Ъbhu, this makes some contextual sense. However, fashioning a river seems beyond even the с╣ЪbhusтАЩ expertise, and, further, in VI.61.13 Sarasvat─л, a river after all, is vibhv├бne kr╠еt─Б╠БтАЬmade for wide extension / wide ranging.тАЭ I think that sense is meant here as well, and there is simply some sly play on the с╣ЪbhuтАЩs name.

I am less certain about what to do with bс╣Ыhaddiv─Б╠Бin c. In the immediately preceding hymn (V.41.19) I take the same form as an attributive adjective with urv├б┼Ы─л: Urva┼Ы─л Bс╣Ыhaddiv─Б тАЬUrva┼Ы─л of lofty heaven.тАЭ Here it could likewise be attributive to Sarasvat─л or it could be a separate goddess. See Klein (I.328-29, 337) on this mild dilemma. If Bс╣Ыhaddiv─Б is a distinct entity, she is featureless, so there is little at stake here.

Griffith

May the House-friends, the cunning-handed Artists, may the Steer’s Wives, the streams carved out by Vibhvan,
And may the fair Ones honour and befriend us, Sarasvati, Brhaddiva, and Raka.

Geldner

Die Hausherren, die K├╝nstler mit geschickter Hand, die von Vibhvan gebildeten Fl├╝sse, die Gattinnen des Bullen, Sarasvat? und Raka vom hohen Himmel, die schmucken, sollen sich gef├дllig zeigen und uns f├╢rdern.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬTo the great protector, (Indra), I offer devout pious praise, new and originated (at this time); to him, the showerer, who, for his daughter (earth), giving form to the rivers, has provided this water for our (use).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

I present to the great one who grants good shelter [=Tvaс╣гс╣нar] wisdom (in the form of) a hymn just newly being born,
to him who, bulging [?] in the belly of his daughter, changing his forms [=Tvaс╣гс╣нar as father of Vi┼Ыvar┼лpa?], made this (world? form?) for us.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The phrase n├бvyas─лс╣Г j─Б╠Бyam─Бnam тАЬthe newer (hymn), being born,тАЭ with comparative of тАШnewтАЩ and the pres. participle seems designed to refer to the current hymn in the process of composition.

Tvaс╣гс╣нar is both the possessor and producer of тАЬall formsтАЭ (cf. I.13.10 tv├бс╣гс╣н─Бram тАж vi┼Ыv├бr┼лpam) and the father of a being called Vi┼Ыvar┼лpa (likewise vi┼Ыv├бr┼лpa- тАШpossessing all formsтАЩ (cf. II.11.19, X.8.9 tv─Бс╣гс╣нr├б- vi┼Ыv├бr┼лpa- with the patronymic tv─Бс╣гс╣нr├б-). In one sense the second hemistich seems to be an attempt to reconcile these two aspects: Tvaс╣гс╣нar as a lone creator god, the fashioner of all forms, тАЬ(ex)changing his formsтАЭ (r┼лp─Б╠Бmin─Бn├бс╕е) as sole agent – but doing so тАЬbulging (?) in the body of his daughterтАЭ (─Бhan─Б╠Бduhit├║r vakс╣г├бn─Бsu)(if thatтАЩs what it means), which introduces a sexual (indeed incestuous) element that would be appropriate to the fathering of a son. On the one hand, we seem to have a model of primitive embryology, with the fetus changing and developing within its motherтАЩs womb; on the other hand, the half-vs. mirrors the later Sanskrit notion that the father enters the body of the mother and is reborn as the son. Unlike the incest of Dyaus and of Praj─Бpati, the story of Tvaс╣гс╣нarтАЩs incest (if thatтАЩs what this is) is otherwise muted and not securely attested elsewhere.

The meaning and etymology of the s-stem ─Бhan├бs- are deeply uncertain. In context it seems to mean тАШswollen, bulging, luxuriant, lubriciousтАЩ. As for the etym. see EWA s.v. and, for a recent etymological attempt, Kulikov in the Lubotsky Fs.

(2018). The word has gained a certain notoriety in IEist discourse because it is argued that it preserves the old suffixal accent of s-stem bahuvr─лhis (see St├╝ber, sstems [2002] 27, 189). However, it is dangerous to pin the reconstruction of a whole category on a word whose meaning, structure, and etymology are radically uncertain.

For disc. of the word, as well as demolition of the accentual theory it is supposed to support, see Jesse Lundquist тАЬ╬▒с╝░╬╜╬┐╧А╬▒╬╕╬о╧В.тАЭ On vakс╣г├бс╣З─Б- тАШbellyтАЩ as a pl. tantum, see comm. ad X.27.16.

My newest song, thought that now springs within me, I offer to the Great, the Sure Protector,
Who made for us this All, in fond love laying each varied form within his Daughter’s bosom.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Despite the position of pr├б, opening a p─Бda that ends with the part.

ukс╣г├бm─Бс╣Зaс╕е, I take the pr├б not with that participle but with immediately preceding p─Бda-final ├нyarti. For one thing, pr├б is found elsewhere with ├нyar- while it is not with тИЪukс╣г, and in addition tmesis of preverb + participle is fairly uncommon (though certainly not unheard of). Geldner and Renou seem to follow the other route, taking it as license to interpr. ├нyarti as intrans. or at least objectless (Geldner тАШheraufziehtтАЩ, Renou тАШsтАЩavanceтАЩ). But ├нyar- is otherwise always transitive, and though we would prefer the two world halves not to be in motion, the point here is that ParjanyaтАЩs thunderstorm is powerful enough to shake them. Witzel Got┼НтАЩs interpr. is like mine.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay this hymn reach up to the presence of the might of the Maruts the youthful sons of Rudra; the desire of riches incites me to holiness; glorify those who go to sacrifice on spotted steeds.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

May this praise reach up to the Marutian troop, to the youthful sons of Rudra.
Desire calls me to wealth with well-being. Praise the unruly ones with dappled horses. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

This trio of vss. echoes vs. 1 and ring-compositionally seems to bring the hymn to a close, with the single p─Бda of 17 and the final vs. 18 tacked on (and indeed the 2nd hemistich of 16: see below). The template is pr├б [HYMN, etc.] [GOD] n┼лn├бm a┼Ыy─Бс╕е, realized in 1ab as тАЬMay the hymn (g─л╠Бс╕е) now reach Varuс╣Зa (etc.).тАЭ In 14ab we again have all the elements, while 15ab omits the initial preverb pr├б in favor of ├║d immediately preceding the verb and omits n┼лn├бm entirely and 16ab reinstates pr├б but still lacks n┼лn├бm: 1ab pr├б тАж v├бruс╣Зam (etc.)тАж g─л╠Бr тАж n┼лn├бm a┼Ыy─Бс╕е 14ab pr├б suс╣гс╣нut├нс╕е тАж iс╕╖├бs p├бtim тАж n┼лn├бm a┼Ыy─Бс╕е 15ab eс╣г├б st├│mo m─Б╠Бrutaс╣Г ┼Ы├бrdhaс╕е (etc.)тАж ├║d a┼Ыy─Бс╕е 16ab pra├нс╣г├б st├│maс╕е pс╣Ыthiv─л╠Бm (etc.) тАж a┼Ыy─Бс╕е The impression given by this sequence of syntactic and lexical parallels – that this is the finale of the hymn – is supported by the fact that the rest of the hymn, 16cd-18, is repeated as15cd-17 in the next hymn, V.43.

Griffith

May this my laud attain the troop of Maruts, those who are youths in act, the Sons of Rudra.
The wish calls me to riches and well-being: praise the unwearied Ones whose steeds are dappled.

Geldner

Jamison Brereton

May this praise reach to earth, to the midspace, to the trees, to the plants, for wealth.
Let every god be easy for me to invoke. Let Mother Earth not set us in disfavor. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes
14-16 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

This trio of vss. echoes vs. 1 and ring-compositionally seems to bring the hymn to a close, with the single p─Бda of 17 and the final vs. 18 tacked on (and indeed the 2nd hemistich of 16: see below). рд╡рдпрдореН рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдиреЛрдГ рдиреВрддрдиреЗрди рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдордиреНрдпреИрд░рдирдиреБрднреВрддреЗрди рдордпреЛрднреБрд╡рд╛ рд╕реБрдЦрд╕реНрдп рднрд╛рд╡рдпрд┐рддреНрд░рд╛ рд╕реБрдкреНрд░рдгреАрддреА рд╢реЛрднрдирдкреНрд░рдгрдпрдирд╡рддрд╛ рдЕрд╡рд╕рд╛ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгреЗрди рд╕рдВ рдЧрдореЗрдо рд╕рдВрдЧрдЪреНрдЫреЗрдорд╣рд┐ ред рд╣реЗ рдЕрдореГрддрд╛ рдЕрдорд░рдгрд╛рд╡рд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдиреМ рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдВ рд░рдпрд┐рдВ рдзрдирдореН рдЖ рд╡рд╣рддрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдпрддрдореН ред рдУрдд рд╡реАрд░рд╛рдиреН рд╕реБрд╡реАрд░реНрдпрд╡рддрдГ рдкреБрддреНрд░рд╛рдирдкрд┐ рдЖ рд╡рд╣рддрдореН ред рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдирд┐ рд╕реМрднрдЧрд╛рдиреНрдпрдкрд┐ рдЖ рд╡рд╣рддрдореН рее рее резреп рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay we ever be participant of the unprecedented, joy-conferring and well-guided protection of the A┼Ыvins; bring to us, immortal (A┼Ыvins), riches, male progeny, and all good things.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

May we come together with the present help of the A┼Ыvins, which is joy itself and provides good guidance.
Here to us bring wealth and here heroes, you two immortals, and here all that brings good fortune.

Griffith

May we obtain the Asvins’ newest favour, and gain their health-bestowing happy guidance.
Bring riches hither unto us, and heroes, and all felicity and joy, Immortals!

Geldner

Wir m├╢chten der neuesten erfreulichen Gnade und der guten F├╝hrung der Asvin teilhaft werden. Bringet uns Reichtum und S├╢hne, alle Gl├╝cksg├╝ter mit, ihr beiden Unsterblichen!

Grassmann

Erlangen m├╢gen wir der Ritter H├╝lfe, die neuste, die erquickt und sicher leitet; O fahret Gut her, fahret her uns Helden, Unsterbliche, und alle Gl├╝ckesg├╝ter.

рдЕрдзрд┐рдордиреНрддреНрд░рдореН (VC)
  • рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡реЗрджреЗрд╡рд╛:
  • рдЕрддреНрд░рд┐рдГ
  • рдирд┐рдЪреГрддреНрддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрдкреН
  • рдзреИрд╡рддрдГ
рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдлрд┐рд░ рдЙрд╕реА рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХреЛ рдХрд╣рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ (рдордпреЛрднреБрд╡рд╛) рд╕реБрдЦ рдХреЗ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЛ (рд╕реБрдкреНрд░рдгреАрддреА) рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддреА рдЧрдИ рдиреАрддрд┐ рдЬрд┐рдирд╕реЗ рдРрд╕реЗ рдЕрдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХ рдФрд░ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢рдХ рдЬрдиреЛ ! рдЬреЛ рдЖрдк рджреЛрдиреЛрдВ (рдирдГ) рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рд░рдпрд┐рдореН) рд▓рдХреНрд╖реНрдореА рдХреЛ (рдЖ, рд╡рд╣рддрдореН) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдХрд░рд╛рдЗрдпреЗ (рдЙрдд) рднреА (рд╡реАрд░рд╛рдиреН) рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрда рд╢реВрд░рддрд╛ рдЖрджрд┐ рдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рдпреБрдХреНрдд рд╢реВрд░рд╡реАрд░ рдЬрдиреЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рдЖ) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдХрд░рд╛рдЗрдпреЗ рдФрд░ рднреА (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдирд┐) рд╕рдореНрдкреВрд░реНрдг (рдЕрдореГрддрд╛) рдирд┐рддреНрдп (рд╕реМрднрдЧрд╛рдирд┐) рд╕реБрдиреНрджрд░ рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рднрд╛рд╡рд░реВрдк рдХреЛ (рдЖ) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдХрд░рд╛рдЗрдпреЗ рдЙрди (рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдиреЛрдГ) рдЕрдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХ рдФрд░ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢рдХреЛрдВ рдХреЗ (рдиреВрддрдиреЗрди) рдирд╡реАрди (рдЕрд╡рд╕рд╛) рд░рдХреНрд╖рдг рд╕реЗ рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧ рд╕рдореНрдкреВрд░реНрдг рдирд┐рддреНрдп рд╕реБрдиреНрджрд░ рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рднрд╛рд╡рд░реВрдкреЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рд╕рдореН, рдЧрдореЗрдо) рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрд╡реЗрдВ реерезреорее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛ ! рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рд░рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдд рдФрд░ рдмреЛрдз рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдП рдЖрдк рд▓реЛрдЧ рд▓рдХреНрд╖реНрдореА рдФрд░ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╕рд╣рд╛рдп рд╕реЗ рд╕рдореНрдкреВрд░реНрдг рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реВрдЬрд┐рдпреЗ реерезреорее рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡реЗрджреЗрд╡ рд░реБрджреНрд░ рдФрд░ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдг рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рдХрд░рдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдЗрд╕ рд╕реЗ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рее рдпрд╣ рдмрдпрд╛рд▓реАрд╕рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рдЙрдиреНрдиреАрд╕рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдордпреЛрднреБрд╡рд╛ рд╕реБрдкреНрд░рдгреАрддреА рдЕрдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХреЛрдкрджреЗрд╢рдХреМ ! рдпреМ рдпреБрд╡рд╛рдВ рдиреЛ рд░рдпрд┐рдорд╛ рд╡рд╣рддрдореБрдд рд╡реАрд░рд╛рдирд╛ рд╡рд╣рддрдордкрд┐ рдЪ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдиреНрдпрдореГрддрд╛ рд╕реМрднрд╛рдЧрд╛рдиреНрдпрд╛ рд╡рд╣рддрдВ рддрдпреЛрд░рд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдиреЛрд░реНрдиреВрддрдиреЗрдирд╛рд╡рд╕рд╛ рд╡рдпрдВ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдиреНрдпрдореГрддрд╛ рд╕реМрднрдЧрд╛рдирд┐ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрдореЗрдо реерезреорее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╕рдореН) (рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдиреЛрдГ) рдЕрдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХреЛрдкрджреЗрд╢рдХрдпреЛрдГ (рдЕрд╡рд╕рд╛) рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгреЗрди (рдиреВрддрдиреЗрди) (рдордпреЛрднреБрд╡рд╛) рд╕реБрдЦрдВ рднрд╛рд╡реБрдХреМ (рд╕реБрдкреНрд░рдгреАрддреА) рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБ рдкреНрд░рдЧрддрд╛ рдиреАрддрд┐рд░реНрдпрд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рддреМ (рдЧрдореЗрдо) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрдпрд╛рдо (рдЖ) (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН (рд░рдпрд┐рдореН) рд╢реНрд░рд┐рдпрдореН (рд╡рд╣рддрдореН) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдпрддрдореН (рдЖ) (рдЙрдд) рдЕрдкрд┐ (рд╡реАрд░рд╛рдиреН) рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрдард╛рдиреН рд╢реВрд░рд╛рдиреН рд╢реМрд░реНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдЧреБрдгреЛрдкреЗрддрд╛рдиреН (рдЖ) (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдирд┐) рд╕рдордЧреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ (рдЕрдореГрддрд╛) рдирд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐ (рд╕реМрднрдЧрд╛рдирд┐) рд╢реЛрднрдирд╛рдирд╛рдореИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рднрд╛рд╡рд░реВрдкрд╛рдгрд┐ реерезреорее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ ! рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрд░рдХреНрд╖рд┐рддрд╛ рдмреЛрдзрд┐рддрд╛рдГ рд╕рдиреНрддреЛ рдпреВрдпрдВ рд╢реНрд░рд┐рдпрдореБрддреНрддрдордордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╕рд╣рд╛рдпреЗрди рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдгреНрдпреИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╛рдгрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрддреЗрддрд┐ реерезреорее рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡реЗрджреЗрд╡рд░реБрджреНрд░рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддрд┐ рджреНрд╡рд┐рдЪрддреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд┐рдВрд╢рддреНрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдореЗрдХреЛрдирд╡рд┐рдВрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рдорд╛рдгрд╕рд╛рдВрдиреЛ! рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВрдХрдбреВрди рд░рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдд рд╡ рдмреЛрдзрд┐рдд рдЭрд╛рд▓реЗрд▓реЗ рддреБрдореНрд╣реА рд▓рдХреНрд╖реНрдореА рд╡ рдЙрддреНрддрдо рд▓реЛрдХрд╛рдВрдЪреНрдпрд╛ рд╕рд╛рд╣реНрдпрд╛рдиреЗ рд╕рдВрдкреВрд░реНрдг рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдп рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдХрд░рд╛. рее резрео рее
